text:
This is a great basic Sausage and Gravy! My husband grew up eating this stuff and introduced it to me about 10 years ago. It is a family staple now. A note on the gravy: DO NOT DRAIN THE SAUSAGE. You need the grease inorder to bring the gravy together, adding butter will drastically change the flavor. We use red pepper flakes and toss it in as the sausage is cooking. You can also use the "hot" flavored sausage to get an extra layer of flavor. Make sure that you completly stir in the flour and alow it to cook with the sausage and grease for a minute or two before addin the milk, this will take out any "pastey taste". Add the milk slowly, I have used skim, 1%, all the way to cream, usually whatever I have on hand. I have found that the less fat your milk has, the less milk you will need to create the gravy! Great on biscuts, toast, cornbread, mashed potatoes, and more...yummmm :)

text:
I didn't have Jimmy Dean crumbles but I did have a roll of the ground sausage I used. I couponed a couple days ago and had a few canisters of whomp biscuits so this was perfect for that. I did add a little red pepper flake. Whole skillet? Gone. Great winter snowy morning breakfast. NOTE: For most white gravy mixes, I use equal amounts butter and flour and make a roux in the skillet before I wisk in the milk. It makes for a better gravy.

text:
Ever since I started using this recipe years ago, I can't eat anyone else's biscuits and gravy (neither can my kids!)  Be prepared to increase the quantity if you have extra people, many will want seconds! Also, stick with Jimmy Dean, (I use the raw ground kind in a tube, HOT is great!) whenever I try a different sausage, I always regret it! I also like to add a couple Tablespoons of butter before the flour.  If you're like me and only have skim milk in the fridge, you can add a can of FF evaporated milk to make it creamier!  I sometimes make huge batches for big camping parties, Just make at home, freeze in gallon ziplocs and reheat at the campsite (take a big bag of pre-baked bisuits).  Good over scrambled eggs too! Tabasco or Cayenne is a nice condiment for me!  Try these, you'll find out that it's easy to make gravy!

text:
Wow. This was my first time ever making biscuits and gravy and it came out awesome, which doesn't happen too often when I try a new recipe. I'm 4 months pregnant and have been really craving this so I found some nitrate free Jimmy Dean ground sausage (in the roll) and used Grands frozen buttermilk biscuits. The only downside was that because I used a whole roll of sausage I had to double the recipe and it made tons - guess I'll be freezing some as my husband won't eat it. Also, it of course took me longer - about 45 mins to make. I used others suggestions and did not drain the sausage but I did add a pat of butter before the flour. Also, I added the flour slowly and cooked for a bit before the milk, then did the same with that. Great consistency, no lumps! This is just as good if not better than the local diner's and no nitrates!

text:
Great recipe!  I just make three small changes.  First, I use turkey sausage instead of pork.  Because he turkey does not produce as many dippings, I add about two tablespoons of butter before making the roux. I also use buttermilk instead of regular milk because it really enhances the flavor of the gravy.  And, contrary to popular belief, it doesn't have to be fattening.   I will also agree with the addition of red pepper flakes if you are looking for a bit of a kick in your gravy.

I used this as a basis for the gravy.. I had buttermilk to use up, so I made biscuits from scratch and I also had 2 large country sausage links already cooked up in the fridge. I diced them up and heat them in the pan, sprinkled them evenly with flour (no measuring) and then added milk until it was the consistency I wanted. Seasoned with salt and pepper to my liking, and there you go.. super quick, delicious meal!

text:
My advice is to take the sausage out once browned, add more oil as needed and then add the flour to the hot oil to cook. Literally the best biscuits and gravy comes from allowing the flour in the pan to cook until it is a dark brick color. Then add back in the sausage and add the milk! The flavor from the darker cooked flour cannot be beat, I wouldn't eat it (or make it) any other way! Sometimes the gravy won't get thick as fast with the sausage, so sprinkling a little more flour on the sausage when you put it back in the pan will help it thicken even more:D

Excellent, simple recipe with delicious results.   Used all natural pork sausage and organic half and half instead of milk. My grandmother taught me to make sausage gravy and I usually just wing it with no recipe, adjusting the proportions of ingredients until it is right.  But I needed to make about 5 cups for an office function so I needed some certainty on the yield so I used this recipe and doubled it.  Used one pound of sausage in a tube and crumbled it as I browned it.  

It came out really well.  I had to add a few TBS of butter and oil as I mixed in the flour to get the right roux consistency, otherwise it would have clumped up too much.  Came out very nice though.

This was really great. I did as some others suggested and melted 3Tbsp of butter with the flour to cook out the flavor. I also used vegetarian sausage wondering how it might work. It was wonderful. Brand matters tho. I used Lightlyfe Gimme Lean Veggie Sausage (14oz). I used olive oil to brown a s break up the sausage then melted the butter added flour stirred the paste for two mins. Then added the milk salt pepper and red pepper flakes and finished the cooking. For biscuits I subbed homemade and used the E-Z Drop Biscuit recipe from All Recipes. Super easy quick and tasty. Next time I will add some sharp cheddar to the biscuit mix!

country:

text:
Great basic recipe, with a few additions & changes this gets a 5+star rating on our opinion.  using my cast iron fry pan: first I added 8 slices of thick cut bacon, drain the grease from the 1st. 4 slice batch, retain the grease from the 2nd. batch, add to that 1 small chopped onion cook until just about translucent, add the sausage cook though and set aside. Add 2 pads of butter to pan, whisk in 1 tablespoon at a time up to 1/4 cup flour, cooking until just golden brown, then add cream/milk about 1/4 cup at a time, add salt & pepper as needed bring to slow boil. in the meantime chop the bacon into small crumbles (the smaller the better), add the bacon crumbles back to cream/milk sauce cook 2 to 4 minutes, then add the sausage onion mixture back to pan, cook another 6 to 10 minutes. make sure you continuously to whisk cream/milk sauce and once you add the meats back stir often. Serve with gravy mixture on top baked hafed cut biscuits.  OMG SOOOO VERY GOOD!!!! the only problem at the portions above this would not serve 8 adults, more like 4.

text:
Great recipe! Important step to avoid LUMPY gravy... after browning sausage, remove the sausage with a slotted spoon and set aside, leaving the grease in the pan. Add flour to the grease... cook a few min then SLOWLY add milk while whisking to avoid lumps. After all of milk is added... then return the meat to gravy.

Every year I go on a golf outing with 8 guys and everyone is responsible for making a dinner or a breakfast. I upscaled this by 4x and had to use 2 pots and it came out great. The only gotcha was it took longer than I expected to thicken the gravy up - I didn't want to burn it but ensuring it gets up to that low light bubbly boil and just stirring a lot and being patient paid off. Fantastic basic recipe!  I was initially concerned that there wasnt enough flour to thicken this but it ended up the perfect thick gravy consistency without becoming sludge.  Would also recommend you add your own seasoning to this as it can be a bit bland.  I added 1/4 tsp poultry seasoning and 1/8 tsp each of marjoram and thyme.  I also added a few red pepper flakes but omit if you use a spicy sausage.  Enjoy finding your favorite flavor combo!

I made sure the flour was on all the turkey sausage before pouring the milk in. Followed the rest of the directions for cooking. Seasoned with salt, pepper, garlic, and a little crushed red pepper. Used Pillsbury Buttery Biscuits. Turned out perfect.

city:

region:

country:
None
text:
I really like this method of gravy making and this has been my go to recipe. I like to make it with chub sausage. My tips: dont drain the sausage and let the flour cook for a few minutes with the sausage before adding the milk. It cooks out the floury pasty flavor and I think makes the gravy taste even better. This gravy tastes even better the next day, so if youre making it for a party you could make the night before and refrigerate it and then just heat it back up on the stove in the morning. I made it for Christmas breakfast and it received a thumbs up. It makes a lot of food without a lot of effort. If the gravy gets too thick just add a splash of milk to thin it back out.

Great recipe, one time I did use a cheaper sausage, don't do that...it was no where near as good. 
Stick with premium brand sausage! (And don't drain the grease)
Also when you add the flour, get it mixed well before adding the milk. And then make sure to turn off the heat BEFORE the gravy gets as thick as you want, because the gravy will continue to thicken in the pan.

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
This is our family favorite breakfast.  I made the Sausage and Gravy in our Instant Pot and it turned out fantastic.

Prepare biscuits according to directions.

Turn the Instant Pot to the saute setting,  add the sausage.  Break up the sausage as it browns.   Do not drain the grease.

Cover the Instant Pot and secure with the lid.  Have the valve set on "sealed".  Set the manual button to 5 minutes.  Then quick release.   Open the lid, stir in flour (we use gluten free all-purpose flour).  When paste, add in milk, salt, pepper and stir well.   Turn the Instant Pot on saute, stir until the gravy is bubbly and thick.   Fantastic.     

I doubled the recipe and used 1/2 tsp salt and 1/2 tsp black pepper.   They make great leftovers.

text:
I learned to make this in college ; I still make it for my family.  I only use 1/2  roll of the Jimmy Dean sausage.  (Jimmy Dean is my favorite too) It's plenty for my family of 4 (I have two tiny teenage girls).  If you have boys then you probably should make more.  I never measure anything.  I add a couple of large spoonfuls of flour after I cook my ground sausage.  This is a recipe that I always make in my iron skillet.  Brown the sausage - I don't drain the sausage because there really isn't ever any grease to drain.  Add the flour  and stir. Cook the flour coated sausage for another minute or two to get rid of the raw flour taste.   Then add the milk until it's the consistency that you would like it to be.   The gravy will get thicker as it cools too.   Add salt /pepper and a few dashes for Louisiana hot sauce.

text:
BOOM! I haven't made sausage gravy and biscuits in probably 20 yrs. Yesterday at our new elite grocery store I saw "BUTTERMILK PORK BREAKFAST SAUSAGE". What?  Gotta have me some. So, I found this recipe and as usual altered it a little.  
After I browned the sausage, it was dry so I added 2T butter. While it melted, I added the flour, and stirred until the flour cooked. Taste it, if it tastes like flour cook more. Then slowly add milk. Next time I will increase milk to 2 3/4 cup.  WONDERFUL!!!!  Worth the calories.

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
This recipe was an excellent base for me to learn from. I made a few changes, though.

The only difference I make is I use bacon for 1/3 of that 9.6 oz of meat so 6.4 oz of sausage and 3.2 oz of bacon. If you're going to make it semi-regularly, what I do is take 2 lbs of sausage and 1 lb of cut up bacon (be sure none of it has been frozen before) and split it up into five 1 quart freezer bags with 6.4 oz of sausage and 3.2 oz of bacon, press it flat, and freeze it. Then it's ready anytime you want it.

The other change I made was adding about 1 tablespoon of butter. Oh, and if you're using bacon, cook the bacon about 3/4 of the way before you add the sausage. Otherwise you'll get undercooked bacon and overcooked sausage.

Last thing, it's really best to use freezer biscuits over refrigerator biscuits. I think they taste way better, almost as good as fresh if you get Grands freezer biscuits. I brush a little vegetable oil on the top and bottom of the biscuit before I bake them. It gives them a slightly crisp edge.

We love this recipe. No matter what sausage I use, it doesn't produce sufficient fat for the roux. So, I always add butter to the drippings from the sausage (for this amount of milk, you'll need 3T of fat). 

I'm trying to be more health conscious, so I substituted a lean turkey sausage, 1% milk, and reduced fat cheese (I add cheese to the gravy before serving), and it was still great.

I've made this twice now. I brown the sausage and add chopped onion and garlic. Then I throw in some red pepper flakes, black pepper, and cayenne pepper. The sausage I use doesn't give off much fat so I add about 2 tbsp butter and sprinkle flour over the entire mess. Cook and stir for a bit to ensure the flour is cooked through and add milk. Taste and add S&P to taste. Fast, easy, and delicious :)

text:
This is a good start to my recipe.  Probably lower in fat as well.  Once in a while treat on holidays or other special occasions.  

I started off with melting butter in my pan,  so the two (2) the sausage wouldn't stick.  I used Country Pride or whatever is on sale.  (Jimmy Deans sausage is too spicy for some who have ARD.)  I heated half and half in the microwave and stirred in the flour with a whisk.  To the milk  and flour mixture I added a couple squirts of Sriracha hot sauce.  This allows for even distribution and avoidance of flour clumping.  In addition,  I added sage and onion powder along with two shakes of salt.   In the past I used two(2) mild and on hot sausage and didn't add hot sause.  I fell in love with the taste of Sriracha.  If it's too spicy I add a couple of teaspoons of sugar to tone it down a bit.

I made the recipe as presented and love it.  It's a classic southern comfort-food.  I use the "Regular" version of the Jimmy Dean sausage, but you can use any of them.  Just don't make the mistake of draining off the small amount of fat from cooking the sausage.  It's needed for the flour to make a roux, and as every good cook already knows, Fat = Flavor!

Finally, I learned how to make a decent sausage gravy!! I used Tennesee Pride sausage that comes in the rolls ( half a tube of mild and 1/2 of a hot)  which is about double what the recipe calls for, but we like our gravy not so runny so we did not double anything else.
